The Logical Structure of the Third Proof
Presents the conditional argument and its proof of connection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the third proof: a conditional argument showing that if God creates human actions, then humans are charged with the impossible.

Core Idea
If God creates every act, humans are commanded to do the impossible.

The third argument is a classic conditional proof. It begins by assuming the position that God is the creator of human actions and then shows that this leads to an impossible consequence—charging humans with what they cannot do. The passage then proves the logical connection (mulāzama) by examining two exhaustive possibilities, both of which are impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional argument
Read the first part of the passage where the author sets up the conditional: if God creates, then the charge is impossible. Identify the antecedent and consequent.
The consequent is 'charging with what one has no power over', which is false.
2
Understand the proof of the connection
The author analyzes two scenarios: either the human has power at the time God creates the act, or at a time when God does not create it. Both are impossible. Grasp why each is contradictory.
The first scenario is impossible because you cannot accomplish what already exists. The second grants the human creative power, contradicting the assumption.
3
See the conclusion
The conclusion is that if God were the creator, the human would have no power at all. But we know we do have power over some actions—this contradiction proves the assumption false.
This sets up the intuitive evidence in the next part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو كان موجد فعل العبد هو الله تعالى ، لكان تكليف العبد بالفعل والترك ، تكليفاً بما لا قدرة له عليه ، واللازم باطل . فالملزوم مثله . بيان الملازمة : أن العبد [ لو كان ] له قدرة [ على الفعل ] لكان إما أن يقدر عليه حال ما خلق الله الفعل ، أو حال ما لم يخلقه الله . والأول محال . لأن ذلك الفعل لما دخل في الوجود بتخليق الله تعالى ، امتنع أن يقدر العبد على تحصيله . لأن تحصيل الحاصل محال . والثاني محال . لأنه تعالى إذا لم يخلق ذلك الفعل ، فلو قدر العبد على تحصيله كان هذا تسليماً ، لكون العبد قادراً على التحصيل والإيجاد ، وذلك ينافي قولنا : إنه غير قادر عليه ، فثبت : [ أن غيره قادر عليه . فثبت ] أن موجد فعل العبد لو كان هو الله تعالى لما كان العبد قادراً على الفعل البتة . وإنما [ قلنا ] أنه قادر على الفعل . لأنه إذا قيل لنا : انتقل من هذا المكان إلى ذلك المكان ، ثم قيل لنا : اخلق شماً وقمراً وسماء وأرضاً . فإنا ببديهة العقل ندرك التفرقة بين البابين ، ونعلم بالضرورة : أنه يمكننا الحركة يمنة ، بدلاً عن يسرة ، وبالعكس . ولا يمكننا خلق الشمس والقمر والسماء والأرض . ولولا كوننا قادرين على أفعالنا ، وإلا لما حصلت هذه التفرقة . وأما إلقاء لفظ الكسب في البين ، فلا فائدة فيه . لأنه إن كان قادرا على التحصيل ، فقد حصل المطلوب . وإن لم يكن قادراً عليه ، فالإلزام المذكور لازم ، ولا واسطة بين القسمين . فكيف ينفع في مثل هذا الموضع القاء لفظة مجهولة في البين ؟
The third proof: if the creator of the servant's act were God, then the servant's being charged with doing and refraining would be a charging with that over which he has no power, and the consequent is false, so the antecedent is likewise false. The proof of the connection: that the servant, if he had power over the act, would either be able to do it at the time when God creates the act, or at the time when God does not create it. The first is impossible, because that act when it has come into existence by God's creation, it is impossible for the servant to have power to accomplish it, for accomplishing what already exists is impossible. The second is impossible, because if God does not create that act, then if the servant were able to accomplish it, this would be an admission that the servant is capable of accomplishment and origination, and that contradicts our statement that he has no power over it. Thus it is established that if the creator of the servant's act were God, the servant would not be able to do the act at all. But we say that he is able to do the act, because when it is said to us: move from this place to that place, and then it is said to us: create a sun, moon, heaven and earth, we discern by the innate reason the difference between the two cases, and we know by necessity that we can move to the right instead of the left and vice versa, and we cannot create the sun, moon, heaven and earth. And were it not that we have power over our actions, this distinction would not occur. As for introducing the term kasb (acquisition), there is no benefit in it, because if he is able to accomplish, then the desired point is conceded; and if he is not able, then the required implication applies, and there is no middle ground between the two divisions. So how in such a place does introducing an unknown term benefit?
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument (al-ḥujja al-thālitha) against the view that God creates human actions. The argument is structured as a conditional proof: if God were the creator of the act, then the human being would be charged with something beyond his capacity. The consequent is false, so the antecedent is false. The proof of the connection (bayān al-mulāzama) is that if the human had power over the act, it would be either at the time when God creates the act or when God does not create it. Both are impossible. The first is impossible because obtaining what already exists is impossible. The second is impossible because if the human could bring about the act when God does not create it, that would mean the human has creative power, contradicting the claim that he has no power. Therefore, if God were the creator, the human would have no power at all. Yet we know by necessity that we have power over some actions, as we distinguish between moving from place to place and creating celestial bodies. The author then dismisses the concept of kasb (acquisition) as a useless term, because either the human has power (and then the point is conceded) or he does not (and the problem remains). There is no middle ground.

Key Terms
قدرة (power)
تحصيل (acquisition)
تخليق (creation)
تكليف (obligation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, why is it impossible for the human to have power over an act at the time God creates it?
A) Because God's power overpowers human power
B) Because the act does not yet exist
C) Because accomplishing what already exists is impossible
D) Because the human does not have the necessary knowledge

Key Takeaway
The third proof shows that the doctrine of divine creation of actions leads to a logical contradiction: it renders human obligation impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused your own sin by feeling that God decreed it? How does this argument challenge that excuse, and what does it demand from you instead?
?
Do you truly believe you are responsible for your actions? If so, why do you sometimes act as if your failures are beyond your control? What would change if you fully internalized this argument?
?
If you affirm that God creates all actions, then how can you take any command of God seriously? Are you living as if you have power to obey, or as if you are a mere puppet? Commit to one honest answer and to live by it today.

Intuitive Evidence and the Dismissal of Kasb
Presents intuitive evidence for human power and dismisses kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses intuitive knowledge to argue for human power over actions and why he rejects the concept of kasb as a meaningless middle ground.

Core Idea
We know by innate reason we can move but not create—proving we have power over our actions.

Having established the logical argument, the author now appeals to our immediate experience. He points out that we intuitively distinguish between actions we can do (like moving) and those we cannot (like creating celestial bodies). This distinction would not exist if we had no power over our actions. He then dismisses the term kasb (acquisition) as an irrelevant escape, because either the human has power or not—there is no middle ground.

Guided Path
1
Read the intuitive argument
Read the part starting with 'وإنما قلنا أنه قادر على الفعل'. Notice the comparison between moving and creating celestial bodies.
This is an appeal to common sense and necessary knowledge.
2
Understand why it proves human power
The author says we know by necessity that we can move to the right or left, but cannot create heavenly bodies. This difference shows we have power over some actions.
If we had no power, we would not be able to distinguish.
3
See the critique of kasb
The author rejects the term kasb as useless because it introduces a false middle ground. Either the human has power (then the argument concedes) or not (then the problem remains).
Kasb is dismissed as an 'unknown term' that does not solve the dilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Sixth Argument: The Conditional Premise
Opens the sixth argument with a conditional premise about divine creation and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opening conditional premise of the sixth argument, which posits that if God creates all human actions including evil, it leads to a theological dilemma.

Core Idea
The sixth argument begins with a conditional: if God creates everything, including evil.

The sixth argument in al-Matalib al-Aliyya tackles a critical objection to divine omnipotence. It opens with a conditional premise that sets up a dilemma: if God is the creator of all human actions, and among them are evil acts, then this leads to a theological problem. This lesson examines that opening premise.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the concise style.
2
Identify the conditional structure
Look for 'لو' which indicates a conditional (if). Notice the two parts: the condition (God creates all actions) and the implication (including ugly acts).
In Arabic, 'لو' often introduces a hypothetical that is contrary to fact or to be examined.
3
Reflect on why evil is highlighted
Ask: why does the argument specifically mention 'ugly acts'? This is central to the objection that God cannot be the source of evil.
The term 'قبائح' refers to morally repugnant acts.

Source Text

Refuting the Fourth Objection: Human Agency and Recognition of God
Author refutes the fourth objection using a logical disjunction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a logical disjunction to refute the objection that denying human creation of actions undermines the recognition of God, prophethood, and the Qur'an.

Core Idea
The objection either depends on its own conclusion or is irrelevant — both options fail.

In this passage, the author addresses a theological objection: if humans do not create their own actions, how can we still affirm the existence of God, prophethood, and the truth of the Qur'an? The objection attempts to tie divine recognition to human agency. The author responds with a clever logical tool — a disjunction — showing that the objection either leads to circular reasoning or is simply disconnected from the original proof. Let's see how this works.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
First, understand what the fourth doubt claims: that without human authorship of actions, the recognition of God, prophethood, and Qur'an become impossible.
2
Identify the two branches
The author presents two possibilities: either the recognition depends on human agency or it does not. Notice the 'either-or' structure.
3
Follow the consequences
If it depends, then proving human agency would require those principles, causing circularity. If it does not depend, then rejecting human agency does not affect those principles.
4
Recognize the refutation
The objection is either circular or irrelevant, so it fails as a critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشبهة الرابعة : وهي قولهم : ولو لم يكن العبد موجـداً لأفعال نفسه ، لما أمكن الاعتراف بالصانع وبالنبوة ويكون القرآن حقاً ، فالجواب : أن الاعتراف بهذه الأصول إن كان موقوفاً على العلم يكون العبد موجداً ، لم يكن إثبات كون العبد موجدا ، بالبناء على تلك الأصول . والا وقع الدور 1 وإن لم . يكن موقوفاً عليه ، لم يلزم من القدح في كون العبد موجداً ، القدح في تلك الأصول . والله أعلم
As for the fourth doubt: It is their statement: If the servant were not the creator (mujid) of his own actions, it would not be possible to acknowledge the Maker, prophethood, and that the Qur'an is true. The answer: That acknowledgement of these principles, if it depends on the knowledge that the servant is the creator, then the proof that the servant is a creator would not be built upon those principles, otherwise circularity would occur. And if it does not depend on it, then discrediting the servant being a creator does not necessitate discrediting those principles. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage addresses the fourth objection (shubha) which argues that if humans do not create their own actions, then the recognition of God (al-Sani'), prophethood, and the truth of the Qur'an would be impossible. The author's response is a logical disjunction. He says: either the recognition of these foundational principles (usul) depends on knowing that the servant is the creator of his actions, or it does not. If it does depend on it, then one cannot prove that the servant is a creator by building on those principles, because that would be circular (dawr). If it does not depend on it, then rejecting the servant's creation of actions does not entail rejecting those principles. Therefore, the objection is either circular or irrelevant. The passage is a clear example of a logical refutation by showing the opponent's argument is self-defeating or inconsequential.

Key Terms
الشبهة الرابعة
العبد موجداً لأفعال نفسه
الاعتراف بالصانع
الدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying human creation of actions logically entails rejecting God, prophethood, and the Qur'an.
Correction: The author shows that this entailment only holds if there is a dependence relation, but that leads to circularity. Without dependence, no entailment exists.

Checkpoint

A) The argument is valid
B) It leads to circularity
C) It proves the Qur'an is false
D) It is based on rational good and evil

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection is refuted by showing it either leads to circularity or is irrelevant to the foundational principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Why Jabr Makes Divine Commands Absurd
The author uses an analogy to refute jabr by showing it makes commands absurd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the analogy of the bound servant demonstrates that the doctrine of jabr (divine compulsion) renders all divine commands meaningless and invalid.

Core Idea
Jabr turns God's commands into absurdities, just like commanding a bound servant to do the impossible.

In this passage, the author uses a powerful analogy to expose the logical flaw in the doctrine of jabr. By comparing divine commands to orders given to a helpless, bound servant, he shows that the jabarī view makes God's commands either impossible or unnecessary. This refutation is crucial for establishing human responsibility within a divinely ordered world.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two distinct scenarios the author presents.
The author uses parallel structure to contrast two cases.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) what God creates in a person is necessary, so commanding it is like telling a bound servant to descend; (2) what God does not create is impossible, so commanding it is like telling a bound servant to return from a fall.
Both cases lead to absurd commands.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that such commands are futile and corrupt, and that the doctrine of jabr invalidates all of God's commands.
This conclusion is the main refutation of jabr.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this analogy is effective: it highlights that without human capacity, command and punishment are meaningless.
The analogy preserves God's wisdom while rejecting compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله تعالى فيه كان واجب الحصول . فكان الأمر به جارياً مجرى ما إذا يقيد الإنسان يدي عبده ورجليه ، ويرميه من شاهق الجبل ، ثم يقول له : انزل ، وإن لم تنزل عذبتك . والذي ما خلقه الله تعالى فيه يكون ممتنع الحصول، فكان الأمر به جاريا مجري ما إذا يقيد يديه ورجليه ويرميه من شاهق الجبل ، ثم يقول له : ارجع وان لم ترجع عذبتك . ومعلوم : أن أمثال هذه التكاليف عبث فاسد . فثبت : أن القول بالجبر يفضي إلى أن تكون جميع تكاليف الله باطلة ضائعة .
What God Most High created in him was necessary to obtain. So the command regarding it was like the case when a person ties the hands and legs of his servant, throws him from a mountain peak, then says to him: 'Descend, and if you do not descend I will punish you.' And that which God Most High did not create in him becomes impossible to obtain, so the command regarding it was like the case when he ties his hands and legs and throws him from a mountain peak, then says to him: 'Return, and if you do not return I will punish you.' And it is known that such commands are futile and corrupt. So it is established that the doctrine of jabr (compulsion) leads to all of God's commands being invalid and wasted.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage refutes the doctrine of al-jabr (divine compulsion) by means of an analogy. The author presents two scenarios: first, if God creates in a person the ability to perform an act, then the command to do it is like telling a bound servant to descend; second, if God does not create the ability, the command is like telling a bound servant to return from a fall. In both cases, the command is absurd because the outcome is predetermined. Thus, the author concludes that believing in jabr makes all of God's commands (takālīf) invalid and wasted.

Key Terms

تكاليف
عبث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the analogy denies God's power to command what He wills.
Correction: The analogy does not deny God's power; it only highlights that commanding the impossible while denying human capacity is absurd and unworthy of God's wisdom. The point is to preserve the meaningfulness of divine commands.

Checkpoint

B) That jabr leads to all divine commands being invalid
C) That the servant is free to obey or disobey
D) That God is unjust

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of jabr makes God's commands either impossible to fulfill or nonsensical, which cannot be attributed to the All-Wise God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author calls such commands 'futile and corrupt.' Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment with a life lived as if His commands were optional or impossible. What would you say? What is one command you have treated lightly that you will take seriously from this day forward?

The Dilemma of Shaytan's Misguidance
Fifth aspect: argument that chain of misguidance makes seeking refuge meaningless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that if shaytan's own misguidance is traced back to Allah, then seeking refuge from shaytan becomes problematic.

Core Idea
If shaytan's misguidance comes from Allah, seeking refuge from him is inconsistent.

This lesson explores the fifth argument against the rationality of seeking refuge from shaytan. The argument presents a dilemma: either shaytan's misguidance comes from another shaytan (leading to infinite regress) or from himself. Each possibility is examined and refuted, culminating in the conclusion that all misguidance ultimately comes from Allah, which undermines the act of seeking refuge. Let's follow the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Get a feel for the argument's flow before diving into details.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main dilemma
The argument presents two possibilities for the source of shaytan's misguidance: from another shaytan (infinite regress) or from himself. Notice how the author sets up this dichotomy.
3
Follow the refutation of infinite regress
The first option leads to an infinite chain, which is declared impossible (muhal). Understand why infinite regress is rejected in kalam.
This is a standard argument against tasalsul.
4
Examine the refutation of self-causation
The second option is refuted with two points: (1) it would allow attributing misguidance to the disbeliever himself, making seeking refuge futile, and (2) it requires an infinite regress of ignorance, which ends in a first ignorance whose origin is unexplained.
The second point is subtle: the mukallaf only chooses ignorance if he mistakes it for knowledge, which itself requires prior ignorance.
5
Understand the conclusion and Quranic support
The only remaining explanation is that shaytan's misguidance comes from Allah. The author cites Qur'an 28:63 to reinforce that all misguidance ultimately traces back to Allah, making seeking refuge from shaytan objectionable (qabih).
Consider the theological implications of this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : إنا إذا قلنا : ضلال الكافر والفاسق ، إنما حصل من وسوسة الشيطان . فإن قلنا : إن ضلال الشيطان، إنما حصل من شيطان آخر . لزم التسلسل . وهو محال . وإن قلنا : حصل من قبل نفسه ، فهو باطل من وجهين : الأول : إنا إذا قلنا ذلك ، فلم لا نقول : إن ضلال الكافر والفاسق إنما حصل من قبل نفسه ، لا من قبل الشيطان ؟ وحينئذ تكون الاستعاذة من الشيطان عبثاً . الثاني : إن المكلف لا يرضى لنفسه البتة باختيار الجهل والكفر ، إلا إذا قيل : إنه إنما اختار ذلك ، لأنه ظن أن ذلك الاعتقاد : علم . لأنه على هذا التقدير لا يمكنه اختيار هذا الجهل ، إلا لسبق جهل آخر . ولا يتسلسل بل ينتهي إلى جهل أول . وحينئذ يعود السؤال في كيفية حصوله . فثبت : أن ضلال ذلك الشيطان إنما حصل بإضلال الله تعالى ، وحينئذ تقبح الاستعاذة بالله من الشيطان ، على هذا التقدير . وإلى هذا التحقيق الإشارة بقوله تعالى : هؤلاء الذين أغوينا . أغويناهم كما غوينا . يعني : إن كانت غوايتهم منا ، فغوايتنا ممن . فالذي أغوانا هو الذي أغوى الكل .
The fifth: Indeed, if we say: the misguidance of the disbeliever and the transgressor occurred only from the whisper of the shaytan. Then if we say: the misguidance of the shaytan occurred only from another shaytan, then an infinite regress (tasalsul) is necessary, and it is impossible. And if we say: it occurred from himself, then it is false from two aspects: First: If we say that, then why do we not say: the misguidance of the disbeliever and the transgressor occurred from himself, not from the shaytan? And then seeking refuge (isti'adhah) from the shaytan would be futile. Second: The responsible person (mukallaf) is never pleased for himself with choosing ignorance and disbelief, unless it is said that he only chose that because he thought that belief was knowledge. For on this assumption, he cannot choose this ignorance except due to a preceding ignorance. And it does not go on infinitely but ends with a first ignorance. And then the question returns regarding how it occurred. So it is established that the misguidance of that shaytan occurred only by Allah's leading astray, and then seeking refuge with Allah from the shaytan is ugly (qabuḥ) on this assumption. And to this verification is indicated by His statement, exalted: 'These are those whom we led astray. We led them astray as we were led astray.' Meaning: If their misguidance is from us, then our misguidance is from whom? So the One who led us astray is the One who led all astray.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument (al-wajh al-khamis) against the rationality of seeking refuge from shaytan. The author (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) argues that if we attribute the misguidance of the disbeliever and transgressor to the whisper of shaytan, then we must explain shaytan's own misguidance. Two possibilities are examined: either shaytan's misguidance comes from another shaytan, leading to an infinite regress (which is impossible), or it comes from himself. The author then refutes the second possibility with two points. First, if shaytan's misguidance is from himself, why not also attribute the disbeliever's misguidance to himself, making seeking refuge futile? Second, a responsible person never chooses ignorance unless he mistakes it for knowledge, but that mistake itself stems from prior ignorance, ending in a first ignorance whose origin remains unexplained. Therefore, the only consistent explanation is that shaytan's misguidance comes from Allah, which implies that seeking refuge from shaytan is morally objectionable (qabih) because it implies seeking refuge from something that Allah Himself causes. The passage concludes by citing Qur'an 28:63 to support the idea that all misguidance ultimately comes from Allah.

Key Terms
التسلسل (tasalsul)
الاستعاذة (isti'adhah)
الوسوسة (waswasah)
المكلف (mukallaf)
الجهل (jahl)
الإضلال (idlaal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeking refuge from shaytan is always a rational action regardless of the source of shaytan's misguidance.
Correction: This argument shows that if shaytan's misguidance is from Allah, then seeking refuge from him becomes inconsistent and morally objectionable.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth argument, what is the consequence of saying that shaytan's misguidance comes from himself?
A) It leads to an infinite regress.
B) It would also allow attributing the disbeliever's misguidance to himself, making seeking refuge futile.
C) It proves that shaytan is not a source of misguidance.
D) It shows that shaytan's misguidance is from Allah.

Key Takeaway
The fifth argument shows that the origin of shaytan's misguidance leads to a dilemma that undermines the rationality of seeking refuge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim,' do you genuinely believe that Allah is the only one who can protect you from shaytan's misguidance, or do you subconsciously think shaytan is an independent agent? Will you now recite isti'adhah with a greater awareness of Allah's absolute power?
?
The argument implies that if shaytan's misguidance is self-caused, then your own sins could also be self-attributed, undermining the excuse 'shaytan made me do it.' Have you ever used shaytan as a scapegoat for your own sins? What would change in your life if you fully accepted personal responsibility for every wrong choice, without deflecting to shaytan? Commit now to repentance without excuses.
?

The Necessary Sequence of Perception: No Room for Shaytan
Razi enumerates the necessary perceptual chain and concludes shaytan has no role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that the deterministic chain from perception to action leaves no causal role for shaytan, making the act of seeking refuge from him rationally unintelligible.

Core Idea
Perception triggers a necessary chain that shaytan cannot break.

In this lesson, we examine a rational argument from Imam al-Razi that challenges the common practice of seeking refuge from shaytan. The argument builds a deterministic model of how perception leads to action, each step following necessarily from the previous. If this chain is truly necessary, then no external agent—shaytan included—can intervene. Let us follow the steps of this argument and see where it leads.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditions for perception
Read the beginning of the passage about the sound eye, facing the visible object, with conditions present and obstacles removed. Note that when these gather, perception is necessary.
This sets the deterministic premise.
2
Identify the sequence of stages
List the stages: perception → knowledge of essence → knowledge of benefit/harm → inclination/aversion → action/avoidance. Each follows necessarily from the previous.
There are four or five stages depending on how you count.
3
Note the claim of necessity
The passage states: 'fatarattubu kulli wahidin min hadhihi al-maratibi 'ala ma qablahu tartubun daruriyyun dhatiyyun'—the ordering is necessary and essential.
This directly excludes any external intervention.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Since shaytan has no influence in any stage, seeking refuge from him becomes rationally unintelligible. Understand why the author argues this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السادس في بيان أن الاستعاذة من الشيطان غير معقولة : إن الحدقة السليمة إذا صارت مقابلة للمرئي، وكان ذلك المرئي قريبا ، والشرائط حاضرة ، والموانع زائلة . فعند اجتماع هذه الأمور يجب حصول الإدراك . وحصول الإدراك مستلزم للعلم بماهية المدرك . والعلم بماهية المدرك يوجب العلم بكونه نافعاً أو ضاراً أو خالياً عنهما . والعلم بكونه نافعا خالياً عن المعارض يوجب الميل إلى تحصيله . والعلم بكونه ضاراً خالياً عن المعارض يوجب النفرة عنه . والميل الجازم يوجب الفعل والنفرة توجب الترك . فترتب كل واحد من هذه المراتب على ما قبله ترتب ضروري ذاتي ، ولا عمل للشيطان فيه . لأن الواجب بذاته لا يصير واجباً بغيره . وثبت : أنه لا تأثير لعمل الشيطان في مرتبة من هذه المراتب . فكيف يستعاذ بالله منه ؟ بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الشيطان ألقى كلاما في خاطر الإنسان وذكره صورة أمر ، بعد أن كان غافلاً ؟ لكنا نقول : صدور هذا التذكير عن الشيطان ، لا بد فيه من المراتب الأربعة المذكورة. فإن كان ذلك الإدراك إنما حصل في قلب ذلك الشيطان ، لأن شيطاناً آخر ذكره ، لزم التسلسل . وإن انتهت هذه الحركات والبواعث والدواعي إلى أنها لم تقع إلا بتخليق الله وبتكوينه فقد صار الكل من الله وحينئذ يرجع حاصل قوله أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم إلى ما صرح به رسول الله وهو قوله : ( أعوذ بك منك ، فوسوسة الشيطان القريب ، وفعل الحق سبحانه هو المبدأ البعيد . لأنه سبحانه مسبب الأسباب ومراتب الكتاب منتهية إليه ، ودرجات الحاجات متصاعدة إليه . ونظيره : قوله تعالى : ( الله يتوفى الأنفس ) ثم قال : ( قل : يتوفاكم ملك الموت ) ثم قال : ( توفته رسلنا ) وما ذاك إلا لما ذكرنا : من أن من الأسباب ما قد تكون قريبة ، وقد تكون بعيدة ، فكذا ههنا
The sixth aspect in explaining that seeking refuge from the shaytan is not rationally intelligible: Indeed, if the sound eye faces the visible object, and that visible object is near, the conditions are present, and the obstacles are removed, then when these matters come together, perception (idrak) necessarily occurs. And the occurrence of perception necessitates knowledge of the essence of the perceived object. And knowledge of the essence of the perceived object necessitates knowledge of whether it is beneficial or harmful or devoid of both. And knowledge of it being beneficial without contrary necessitates inclination (mayl) to acquire it. And knowledge of it being harmful without contrary necessitates aversion (nufrah) from it. And decisive inclination necessitates action, and aversion necessitates avoidance. So the ordering of each of these stages upon what precedes it is a necessary, essential ordering, and there is no action of the shaytan in it. Because that which is necessary by itself does not become necessary by another. And it is established that the shaytan's action has no influence in any of these stages. So how can one seek refuge with Allah from him? It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the shaytan casts speech into the human's mind and reminds him of the image of a thing after he had been heedless? But we say: The occurrence of this reminding from the shaytan necessarily involves the four mentioned stages. For if that perception occurred in the heart of that shaytan because another shaytan reminded him, then an infinite regress is necessary. And if these movements, motives, and inclinations end only by Allah's creation (takhliq) and His bringing into being (takwin), then everything becomes from Allah. And then the upshot of his saying 'I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan' returns to what the Messenger of Allah affirmed, which is his saying: 'I seek refuge with You from You.' So the whisper of the near shaytan, and the act of the Truth, exalted, is the distant beginning. Because He, exalted, is the cause of causes (musabbib al-asbab), and the degrees of the book end with Him, and the levels of needs ascend to Him. And its analogy is His statement, exalted: 'Allah takes the souls' then He said: 'Say: The angel of death takes you' then He said: 'Our messengers take him.' And that is only for what we mentioned: that among causes there are those that are near and those that are far, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument against the intelligibility of seeking refuge from shaytan. It describes a deterministic chain of perception leading to action: when the eye faces an object with proper conditions, perception necessarily occurs, followed by knowledge of the object's essence, then knowledge of its benefit or harm, then inclination or aversion, then action or avoidance. Each step follows necessarily from the previous, leaving no causal role for any external agent like shaytan. The author states that the necessary (al-wajib bi-dhatihi) does not become necessary by another, so shaytan cannot intervene. The passage then addresses an objection: could shaytan not simply remind a heedless person? The response is that this reminder itself would require the same four-stage perceptual process in shaytan, leading either to infinite regress (if another shaytan reminds him) or to Allah as the ultimate creator of all movements and motives. Thus, everything returns to Allah, and the Prophet's saying 'I seek refuge with You from You' is invoked. The argument concludes by comparing to the Qur'anic references to different agents of death (Allah, Angel of Death, messengers), distinguishing between near and distant causes, all ultimately traced back to Allah as the cause of causes.

Key Terms
الإدراك (idrak)
العلم بالمنفعة والمضرة
الميل (mayl)
النفرة (nufrah)
الترتب الضروري (al-taratub al-daruri)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Shaytan can influence the perceptual process directly.
Correction: The passage argues that the perceptual chain is necessary and essential, leaving no causal opening for any external agent.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth argument, what does the necessary ordering of perception imply about the shaytan's role?
A) The shaytan can influence the final action but not the perception.
B) The shaytan has no influence in any stage of the perceptual chain.
C) The shaytan is responsible for the initial perception.
D) The shaytan only affects the inclination, not the perception.

Key Takeaway
The perceptual chain from vision to action is necessary and essential, leaving no causal role for shaytan, thereby making seeking refuge from him rationally unintelligible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perceive something attractive and feel an immediate desire, do you instinctively blame shaytan for that desire? After reading Razi's argument, would you instead acknowledge that the desire is a necessary consequence of your own perception? How might this change how you respond to temptation?
?
Razi claims that the chain from perception to action is necessary and essential, leaving no room for shaytan. If that is true, then what role does your own knowledge and judgment play in your sinful actions? Are you willing to accept responsibility for the inclinations you act upon, rather than attributing them to external whispers?
?
If seeking refuge from shaytan in the moment of perception is 'rationally unintelligible', then what should your prayer be? Would you instead ask Allah to change your perception itself, or to guide your knowledge of benefit and harm? What would that mean for how you approach your daily struggles?

Objection and Resolution: Even Shaytan's Reminder Traces Back to Allah
Razi answers the objection and shows that all actions, including shaytan's, trace back to Allah as the cause of causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that shaytan can simply remind a heedless person fails, leading to the conclusion that all actions ultimately originate from Allah.

Core Idea
Every act, even shaytan's, is part of a chain ending with Allah.

Having established that the perceptual chain leaves no room for shaytan, a possible objection arises: could shaytan not simply cast a thought into the mind of a heedless person? In this lesson, we examine Razi's response. He argues that this reminder itself would require the same four-stage perceptual process in shaytan, leading either to an infinite regress or to Allah as the ultimate creator. The passage then presents a profound conclusion: everything returns to Allah, and seeking refuge from shaytan ultimately means seeking refuge from Allah's own creation—hence the Prophet's prayer 'I seek refuge with You from You.'

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection: why can't we say shaytan simply throws a thought into the human mind after heedlessness?
The objection tries to bypass the deterministic chain by positing a direct mental influence.
2
Understand the response with two branches
The response says that for shaytan to remind, he must have undergone the same four stages of perception. If another shaytan reminded him, infinite regress; if not, then the ultimate cause is Allah's creation (takhliq and takwin).
Both branches lead to Allah as the ultimate cause.
3
Reflect on the analogy with death verses
Read the analogy: Allah taking souls, then Angel of death, then messengers. Just as near and far causes are distinguished, so shaytan is a near cause but Allah is the far cause.
This shows that even when shaytan appears to act, the real agent is Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السادس في بيان أن الاستعاذة من الشيطان غير معقولة : إن الحدقة السليمة إذا صارت مقابلة للمرئي، وكان ذلك المرئي قريبا ، والشرائط حاضرة ، والموانع زائلة . فعند اجتماع هذه الأمور يجب حصول الإدراك . وحصول الإدراك مستلزم للعلم بماهية المدرك . والعلم بماهية المدرك يوجب العلم بكونه نافعاً أو ضاراً أو خالياً عنهما . والعلم بكونه نافعا خالياً عن المعارض يوجب الميل إلى تحصيله . والعلم بكونه ضاراً خالياً عن المعارض يوجب النفرة عنه . والميل الجازم يوجب الفعل والنفرة توجب الترك . فترتب كل واحد من هذه المراتب على ما قبله ترتب ضروري ذاتي ، ولا عمل للشيطان فيه . لأن الواجب بذاته لا يصير واجباً بغيره . وثبت : أنه لا تأثير لعمل الشيطان في مرتبة من هذه المراتب . فكيف يستعاذ بالله منه ؟ بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الشيطان ألقى كلاما في خاطر الإنسان وذكره صورة أمر ، بعد أن كان غافلاً ؟ لكنا نقول : صدور هذا التذكير عن الشيطان ، لا بد فيه من المراتب الأربعة المذكورة. فإن كان ذلك الإدراك إنما حصل في قلب ذلك الشيطان ، لأن شيطاناً آخر ذكره ، لزم التسلسل . وإن انتهت هذه الحركات والبواعث والدواعي إلى أنها لم تقع إلا بتخليق الله وبتكوينه فقد صار الكل من الله وحينئذ يرجع حاصل قوله أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم إلى ما صرح به رسول الله وهو قوله : ( أعوذ بك منك ، فوسوسة الشيطان القريب ، وفعل الحق سبحانه هو المبدأ البعيد . لأنه سبحانه مسبب الأسباب ومراتب الكتاب منتهية إليه ، ودرجات الحاجات متصاعدة إليه . ونظيره : قوله تعالى : ( الله يتوفى الأنفس ) ثم قال : ( قل : يتوفاكم ملك الموت ) ثم قال : ( توفته رسلنا ) وما ذاك إلا لما ذكرنا : من أن من الأسباب ما قد تكون قريبة ، وقد تكون بعيدة ، فكذا ههنا
The sixth aspect in explaining that seeking refuge from the shaytan is not rationally intelligible: Indeed, if the sound eye faces the visible object, and that visible object is near, the conditions are present, and the obstacles are removed, then when these matters come together, perception (idrak) necessarily occurs. And the occurrence of perception necessitates knowledge of the essence of the perceived object. And knowledge of the essence of the perceived object necessitates knowledge of whether it is beneficial or harmful or devoid of both. And knowledge of it being beneficial without contrary necessitates inclination (mayl) to acquire it. And knowledge of it being harmful without contrary necessitates aversion (nufrah) from it. And decisive inclination necessitates action, and aversion necessitates avoidance. So the ordering of each of these stages upon what precedes it is a necessary, essential ordering, and there is no action of the shaytan in it. Because that which is necessary by itself does not become necessary by another. And it is established that the shaytan's action has no influence in any of these stages. So how can one seek refuge with Allah from him? It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the shaytan casts speech into the human's mind and reminds him of the image of a thing after he had been heedless? But we say: The occurrence of this reminding from the shaytan necessarily involves the four mentioned stages. For if that perception occurred in the heart of that shaytan because another shaytan reminded him, then an infinite regress is necessary. And if these movements, motives, and inclinations end only by Allah's creation (takhliq) and His bringing into being (takwin), then everything becomes from Allah. And then the upshot of his saying 'I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan' returns to what the Messenger of Allah affirmed, which is his saying: 'I seek refuge with You from You.' So the whisper of the near shaytan, and the act of the Truth, exalted, is the distant beginning. Because He, exalted, is the cause of causes (musabbib al-asbab), and the degrees of the book end with Him, and the levels of needs ascend to Him. And its analogy is His statement, exalted: 'Allah takes the souls' then He said: 'Say: The angel of death takes you' then He said: 'Our messengers take him.' And that is only for what we mentioned: that among causes there are those that are near and those that are far, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument against the intelligibility of seeking refuge from shaytan. It describes a deterministic chain of perception leading to action: when the eye faces an object with proper conditions, perception necessarily occurs, followed by knowledge of the object's essence, then knowledge of its benefit or harm, then inclination or aversion, then action or avoidance. Each step follows necessarily from the previous, leaving no causal role for any external agent like shaytan. The author states that the necessary (al-wajib bi-dhatihi) does not become necessary by another, so shaytan cannot intervene. The passage then addresses an objection: could shaytan not simply remind a heedless person? Thus, everything returns to Allah, and the Prophet's saying 'I seek refuge with You from You' is invoked. The argument concludes by comparing to the Qur'anic references to different agents of death (Allah, Angel of Death, messengers), distinguishing between near and distant causes, all ultimately traced back to Allah as the cause of causes.

Seventh Argument: Purpose of Isti'adhah
Seventh aspect: analyzing purpose of seeking refuge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the purpose of seeking refuge (isti'adhah) implies theological commitments about divine decrees, enablement, and the source of faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
Seeking refuge reveals theological assumptions about who controls faith.

This lesson examines the seventh argument from the text, which analyzes the purpose of seeking refuge. The author breaks down the possible intentions behind isti'adhah and shows that each possibility carries implications about divine causality and human agency. Even though the passage is incomplete, it offers a glimpse into the theological reasoning about faith and disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the dichotomy
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author begins with a dichotomy: either the purpose is religious interests or worldly interests.
This sets up the logical structure of the argument.
2
Identify the three subcategories of religious interests
Within religious interests, the author lists three possibilities: divine decrees (al-aqdar), enablement (al-tamkin), and attainment of faith (tahsil al-iman). Recognize each one.
The third is mentioned but not elaborated in this excerpt.
3
Understand the critique of the Mu'tazila position
The author notes that divine decrees are already present according to the Mu'tazila, and questions why seeking them would be impermissible. This is a rhetorical move.
This critiques the Mu'tazila view on predestination.
4
Reflect on the implication of seeking enablement
The author states that seeking enablement (al-tamkin) implies an admission that faith and disbelief are from Allah. This is a key theological point.
This connects isti'adhah to the doctrine of divine causality.
5
Consider the incomplete discussion of worldly interests
The passage cuts off when beginning to discuss worldly interests. Reflect on what might follow based on the pattern.
The lesson is limited by the excerpt, but the logic can be extended.

الوجه السابع : إن المقصود من الاستعاذة . إما أن يكون طلب مصالح الدين ، أو طلب مصالح الدنيا . فإن كان الأول فالمطلوب : إما الأقدار ، أو التمكين ، أو تحصيل الإيمان . أما الأول فهو حاصل عند المعتزلة . فلم لا يجوز طلبه ؟ وأما الثاني فذاك اعتراف بأن الإيمان والكفر من الله . وأما مصالح الدنيا
The seventh aspect: Indeed, the intended purpose of seeking refuge (isti'adhah) is either the seeking of religious interests or the seeking of worldly interests. If it is the first, then what is sought is either divine decrees (al-aqdar), or enablement (al-tamkin), or the attainment of faith (iman). As for the first, it is already present according to the Mu'tazila. So why is it not permissible to seek it? As for the second, that is an admission that faith and disbelief are from Allah. As for worldly interests...
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage introduces the seventh aspect, which discusses the purpose of seeking refuge. It poses a dichotomy: either the seeker desires religious interests or worldly ones. If religious, the author breaks it down into three possibilities: seeking divine decrees (al-aqdar), seeking enablement (al-tamkin), or seeking the attainment of faith (tahsil al-iman). The passage notes that for the Mu'tazila, divine decrees are already present, so seeking them would be permissible. The second possibility, seeking enablement, is presented as an admission that faith and disbelief come from Allah. The third possibility (attainment of faith) is not elaborated before the text cuts off. The worldly interests branch is also left incomplete. Despite its brevity, this argument begins to show that the very act of seeking refuge implies theological commitments about divine causality.

Correction: This argument shows that even the act of seeking refuge implies specific theological commitments about the source of faith and disbelief, and about divine causality.

The Four Stages of Action and Satan's Impotence
Enumerates the four stages of action and denies Satan's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four necessary stages that precede any voluntary action and why Satan cannot influence them.

Core Idea
Satan cannot act where necessity governs.

The argument begins by laying out the psychological and rational steps that lead to any deliberate human action: knowledge, inclination, resolve, and action. These stages are linked by necessary causality, not by Satan's intervention. This lesson unpacks that sequence and its implications for the doctrine of isti'adhah.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the four stages
Read the passage and identify the four stages: knowledge (benefit/harm), inclination/aversion, firm resolve (jāzim), and action/abandonment.
Notice that each stage is defined in terms of its preceding condition.
2
Understand the necessity
The text states that the ordering is 'necessary and essential' (ḍarūrī dhātī). Think about what makes each step follow from the previous one.
The necessity is intrinsic, not caused by external factors.
3
Grasp the exclusion of Satan
Since the sequence is necessary, nothing external can change it. The author argues that 'the necessary in itself does not become necessary through another,' so Satan cannot be the cause of any stage.
This is a logical argument against Satan's agency.
4
Connect to seeking refuge
If Satan has no role, why seek refuge from him? This sets up the problem that the next lessons will address.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم بكونه نافعاً أو ضاراً أو خالياً عنهما . والعلم بكونه نـافـعـا خـاليـاً عن المعارض يوجب الميل إلى تحصيله . والعلم بكونه ضاراً خالياً عن المعارض يوجب النفرة عنه . والميل الجازم يوجب الفعل والنفرة توجب الترك . فترتب كل واحد من هذه المراتب على ما قبله ترتب ضروري ذاتي ، ولا عمل للشيطان فيه . لأن الواجب بذاته لا يصير واجباً بغيره . وثبت : أنه لا تأثير لعمل الشيطان في مرتبة من هذه المراتب . فكيف يستعاذ بالله منه ؟ بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الشيطان ألقى كلاما في خاطر الإنسان وذكره صورة أمر ، بعد أن كان غافلاً ؟ لكنا نقول : صدور هذا التذكير عن الشيطان ، لا بد فيه من المراتب الأربعة المذكورة. فإن كان ذلك الإدراك إنما حصل في قلب ذلك الشيطان ، لأن شيطاناً آخر ذكره ، لزم التسلسل . وإن انتهت هذه الحركات والبواعث والدواعي إلى أنها لم تقع إلا بتخليق الله وبتكوينه فقد صار الكل من الله وحينئذ يرجع حاصل قوله أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم إلى ما صرح به رسول الله وهو قوله : ( أعوذ بك منك ) فوسوسة الشيطان القريب ، وفعل الحق سبحانه هو المبدأ البعيد . لأنه سبحانه مسبب الأسباب ومراتب الكتاب منتهية إليه ، ودرجات الحاجات متصاعدة إليه هي المبدأ ونظيره : قوله تعالى : ( الله يتوفى الأنفس ) ثم قال : ( قل : يتوفاكم ملك الموت ) ثم قال : ( توفته رسلنا ) وما ذاك إلا لما ذكرنا : من أن من الأسباب ما قد تكون قريبة ، وقد تكون بعيدة ، فكذا ههنا الوجه السابع : إن المقصود من الاستعاذة . إما أن يكون طلب مصالح الدين ، أو طلب مصالح الدنيا . فإن كان الأول فالمطلوب : إما الأقدار ، أو التمكين ، أو تحصيل الإيمان . أما الأول فهو حاصل عند المعتزلة . فلم لا يجوز طلبه ؟ وأما الثاني فذاك اعتراف بأن الإيمان والكفر من الله . وأما مصالح الدنيا فهي خسيسة . فلا يجوز أن يجعل المكلف طلبها ، مقدمة لإقدامه على جميع العبادات والطاعات . والله أعلم . فهذا خلاصة المباحث الواقعة في ماهية الاستعاذة ، على المذهبين وبالله التوفيق
Knowledge of a thing being beneficial or harmful or devoid of both. And knowledge of it being beneficial without opposition necessitates inclination to acquire it. And knowledge of it being harmful without opposition necessitates aversion from it. And firm inclination necessitates action, and aversion necessitates abandonment. So the ordering of each of these stages upon what precedes it is necessary and essential, and Satan has no action in it. Because the necessary in itself does not become necessary through another. And it is established that Satan's action has no effect in any of these stages. So how can one seek refuge in Allah from him? It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that Satan cast a word into the heart of a person and reminded him of an image of a matter after he had been heedless? But we say: The occurrence of this reminder from Satan inevitably requires the four mentioned stages. If that cognition occurred in the heart of that Satan because another Satan reminded him, then vicious regress (التسلسل) would be necessary. And if these movements, motivations, and inclinations ended only by Allah's creation and constitution, then everything becomes from Allah. Then the outcome of his saying 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Satan' goes back to what the Messenger of Allah declared, namely his saying: 'I seek refuge in You from You.' So the whisper of the near Satan, and the act of the Exalted Truth is the remote beginning. Because He, exalted, is the cause of causes, and the stages of the decree end with Him, and the degrees of needs ascend to Him. It is the beginning. And its analogue is His saying: 'Allah takes the souls', then He said: 'Say: The angel of death takes you', then He said: 'Our messengers take him.' And that is only for what we mentioned: that among causes some are near and some are far, so here likewise. The seventh aspect: The purpose of seeking refuge is either to seek religious benefits or worldly benefits. If the first, then what is sought is either divine decrees, or empowerment, or acquisition of faith. As for the first, it is already obtained among the Mu'tazila, so why is it not permissible to seek it? As for the second, that is an admission that faith and disbelief are from Allah. As for worldly benefits, they are base, so it is not permissible for the obligated person to make seeking them a prerequisite for undertaking all acts of worship and obedience. And Allah knows best. This is the summary of the investigations concerning the essence of seeking refuge, according to the two schools. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a complex argumentative unit defending the Ash'ari view that all human actions, including the response to Satan's whispers, are ultimately caused by Allah alone. It begins by analyzing the four stages that precede any voluntary action: knowledge of the action's benefit/harm, inclination (if beneficial) or aversion (if harmful), firm resolve, and finally action or abandonment. The author asserts that each stage necessarily follows the previous one, and Satan has no effect on these stages because a necessary thing cannot become necessary through another. Since Satan has no influence, seeking refuge from him seems futile. The author then addresses an objection: could Satan not simply remind a person of an action, without affecting the stages? The reply shows that even this reminder would require the same four stages in Satan himself, leading to an infinite regress unless it is all created by Allah. Thus, all is from Allah, and the phrase 'I seek refuge in You from You' acknowledges that the ultimate cause is Allah. The author provides an analogy with verses about death: Allah takes souls, but the angel of death is the near cause. Finally, the seventh point distinguishes between seeking religious or worldly benefits, arguing that religious benefits already come from Allah (even Mu'tazila agree) and seeking them admits divine control, while worldly benefits are too base to be the primary aim of worship. The passage concludes the discussion on isti'adha scross two schools.

Key Terms
العلم
الميل
النفرة
الترتب الضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Satan directly influences human actions by causing inclinations or decisions.
Correction: The passage shows that the sequence of stages is necessary and intrinsic; Satan cannot cause any of them because necessity cannot come from an external source.

Checkpoint
Why, according to the passage, does Satan have no influence on the four stages?
A) Because Satan is not a real entity.
B) Because each stage necessarily follows its predecessor, and necessity cannot come from another.
C) Because humans are free to choose independently of any cause.
D) Because the stages are random.

Key Takeaway
The four stages of action are necessarily linked, and Satan cannot intervene in this natural causality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes blame Satan for your own sins, thinking he made you do it? After this lesson, do you still hold that excuse? How will you take full responsibility now?
?
If every action you take is preceded by knowledge and inclination that are intrinsically necessary, what is your duty regarding the knowledge you seek? Are you indifferent to learning what benefits or harms you spiritually?
?
The passage declares Satan has no effect on the stages of action. Where does this leave your daily supplications for protection from him? Is your refuge in Allah merely a ritual, or does it reflect a deeper reliance on the One who truly controls all causation?

Causality and Created Things
advanced
10 min
Refuting Satan's Influence: Infinite Regress and Divine Causality
Refutes objection about Satan's reminder, using infinite regress and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that Satan merely reminds humans, and how the response exposes an infinite regress unless all action is ultimately from Allah.

Core Idea
Even a reminder from Satan requires divine creation.

An objector might concede that Satan has no direct influence on the necessary stages but could still 'remind' or 'prompt' an action. The author refutes this by showing that such a reminder would itself require the same four stages in Satan, leading to an infinite regress unless Allah is the ultimate cause. This lesson traces that argument and the analogy with the verses about death.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector proposes that Satan might simply remind a heedless person of an action, without affecting the stages.
This is a plausible counterargument.
2
Follow the response
The author argues that for Satan to remind, he himself must go through the four stages. If that cognition came from another Satan, we get infinite regress.
Infinite regress (tasalsul) is impossible in kalam.
3
See the resolution
The only way to avoid regress is that all motivations and actions are directly created by Allah. Hence, everything is from Allah.
This leads to the famous statement 'I seek refuge in You from You'.
4
Appreciate the analogy
The author compares this to the Quranic verses about death: Allah, the angel of death, and messengers all have roles, but ultimate causality is Allah's.
This illustrates the concept of 'near cause' (al-sabab al-qarīb) vs 'remote beginning' (al-mabdaʿ al-baʿīd).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم بكونه نافعاً أو ضاراً أو خالياً عنهما . والعلم بكونه نـافـعـا خـاليـاً عن المعارض يوجب الميل إلى تحصيله . والعلم بكونه ضاراً خالياً عن المعارض يوجب النفرة عنه . والميل الجازم يوجب الفعل والنفرة توجب الترك . فترتب كل واحد من هذه المراتب على ما قبله ترتب ضروري ذاتي ، ولا عمل للشيطان فيه . لأن الواجب بذاته لا يصير واجباً بغيره . وثبت : أنه لا تأثير لعمل الشيطان في مرتبة من هذه المراتب . فكيف يستعاذ بالله منه ؟ بقي أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الشيطان ألقى كلاما في خاطر الإنسان وذكره صورة أمر ، بعد أن كان غافلاً ؟ لكنا نقول : صدور هذا التذكير عن الشيطان ، لا بد فيه من المراتب الأربعة المذكورة. فإن كان ذلك الإدراك إنما حصل في قلب ذلك الشيطان ، لأن شيطاناً آخر ذكره ، لزم التسلسل . وإن انتهت هذه الحركات والبواعث والدواعي إلى أنها لم تقع إلا بتخليق الله وبتكوينه فقد صار الكل من الله وحينئذ يرجع حاصل قوله أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم إلى ما صرح به رسول الله وهو قوله : ( أعوذ بك منك ) فوسوسة الشيطان القريب ، وفعل الحق سبحانه هو المبدأ البعيد . لأنه سبحانه مسبب الأسباب ومراتب الكتاب منتهية إليه ، ودرجات الحاجات متصاعدة إليه هي المبدأ ونظيره : قوله تعالى : ( الله يتوفى الأنفس ) ثم قال : ( قل : يتوفاكم ملك الموت ) ثم قال : ( توفته رسلنا ) وما ذاك إلا لما ذكرنا : من أن من الأسباب ما قد تكون قريبة ، وقد تكون بعيدة ، فكذا ههنا الوجه السابع : إن المقصود من الاستعاذة . إما أن يكون طلب مصالح الدين ، أو طلب مصالح الدنيا . فإن كان الأول فالمطلوب : إما الأقدار ، أو التمكين ، أو تحصيل الإيمان . أما الأول فهو حاصل عند المعتزلة . فلم لا يجوز طلبه ؟ وأما الثاني فذاك اعتراف بأن الإيمان والكفر من الله . وأما مصالح الدنيا فهي خسيسة . فلا يجوز أن يجعل المكلف طلبها ، مقدمة لإقدامه على جميع العبادات والطاعات . والله أعلم . فهذا خلاصة المباحث الواقعة في ماهية الاستعاذة ، على المذهبين وبالله التوفيق
Knowledge of a thing being beneficial or harmful or devoid of both. And knowledge of it being beneficial without opposition necessitates inclination to acquire it. And knowledge of it being harmful without opposition necessitates aversion from it. And firm inclination necessitates action, and aversion necessitates abandonment. So the ordering of each of these stages upon what precedes it is necessary and essential, and Satan has no action in it. Because the necessary in itself does not become necessary through another. And it is established that Satan's action has no effect in any of these stages. So how can one seek refuge in Allah from him? It remains to be said: Why is it not permissible to say that Satan cast a word into the heart of a person and reminded him of an image of a matter after he had been heedless? But we say: The occurrence of this reminder from Satan inevitably requires the four mentioned stages. If that cognition occurred in the heart of that Satan because another Satan reminded him, then vicious regress (التسلسل) would be necessary. And if these movements, motivations, and inclinations ended only by Allah's creation and constitution, then everything becomes from Allah. Then the outcome of his saying 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Satan' goes back to what the Messenger of Allah declared, namely his saying: 'I seek refuge in You from You.' So the whisper of the near Satan, and the act of the Exalted Truth is the remote beginning. Because He, exalted, is the cause of causes, and the stages of the decree end with Him, and the degrees of needs ascend to Him. It is the beginning. And its analogue is His saying: 'Allah takes the souls', then He said: 'Say: The angel of death takes you', then He said: 'Our messengers take him.' And that is only for what we mentioned: that among causes some are near and some are far, so here likewise. The seventh aspect: The purpose of seeking refuge is either to seek religious benefits or worldly benefits. If the first, then what is sought is either divine decrees, or empowerment, or acquisition of faith. As for the first, it is already obtained among the Mu'tazila, so why is it not permissible to seek it? As for the second, that is an admission that faith and disbelief are from Allah. As for worldly benefits, they are base, so it is not permissible for the obligated person to make seeking them a prerequisite for undertaking all acts of worship and obedience. And Allah knows best. This is the summary of the investigations concerning the essence of seeking refuge, according to the two schools. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a complex argumentative unit defending the Ash'ari view that all human actions, including the response to Satan's whispers, are ultimately caused by Allah alone. It begins by analyzing the four stages that precede any voluntary action: knowledge of the action's benefit/harm, inclination (if beneficial) or aversion (if harmful), firm resolve, and finally action or abandonment. The author asserts that each stage necessarily follows the previous one, and Satan has no effect on these stages because a necessary thing cannot become necessary through another. Since Satan has no influence, seeking refuge from him seems futile. The author then addresses an objection: could Satan not simply remind a person of an action, without affecting the stages? The reply shows that even this reminder would require the same four stages in Satan himself, leading to an infinite regress unless it is all created by Allah. Thus, all is from Allah, and the phrase 'I seek refuge in You from You' acknowledges that the ultimate cause is Allah. The author provides an analogy with verses about death: Allah takes souls, but the angel of death is the near cause. Finally, the seventh point distinguishes between seeking religious or worldly benefits, arguing that religious benefits already come from Allah (even Mu'tazila agree) and seeking them admits divine control, while worldly benefits are too base to be the primary aim of worship. The passage concludes the discussion on isti'adha scross two schools.

Key Terms
التسلسل
المبدأ البعيد
مسبب الأسباب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Satan can remind humans without any divine involvement.
Correction: The argument shows that even a reminder requires a causal chain that ultimately depends on Allah; otherwise infinite regress occurs.

Checkpoint
What does the argument say would happen if Satan's reminder came from another Satan?
A) It would be impossible because Satan cannot remind.
B) It would lead to an infinite regress (tasalsul).
C) It would be a valid cause.
D) It would prove Satan's independence.

Key Takeaway
The reminder objection collapses into infinite regress unless all causality is traced back to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sense a whisper of evil in your heart, do you truly believe that both the whisper and your refuge from it are from Allah? How does this conviction shape your plea ‘A‘ūdhu billāhi mina al-shayṭān al-rajīm’?
?
If every movement and motivation, even from Satan, is created by Allah, how does that change the way you view your own sinful inclinations? Are you more prone to blame others or to turn back to Allah in humility?
?
The Prophet ﷺ taught us to say ‘I seek refuge in You from You.’ Have you ever felt the weight of those words? In what specific moments of your life does this realization challenge your self-reliance or your assumptions about good and evil?

The Purpose of Seeking Refuge: Religious vs Worldly Benefits
Distinguishes purposes of isti'adhah and argues for divine origin of religious benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between seeking religious and worldly benefits in isti'adhah, and why the former acknowledges divine control while the latter is base.

Core Idea
Seeking refuge is ultimately an admission that all is from Allah.

The final section of the passage examines the purpose (maqṣūd) of seeking refuge from Satan. It distinguishes between seeking religious benefits (maṣāliḥ al-dīn) and worldly benefits (maṣāliḥ al-dunyā). The author argues that if one seeks religious benefits, those benefits are already from Allah (even Mu'tazila agree), and the act of seeking is an implicit confession that faith and disbelief are from Allah. Worldly benefits, being base, should not be the primary aim of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two purposes
The passage states that the purpose of seeking refuge is either religious or worldly benefits.
These are the two main categories.
2
Analyze religious benefits
Under religious benefits, three sub-aims are listed: divine decrees (aqdār), empowerment (tamkīn), and acquisition of faith (taḥṣīl al-īmān).
The first, divine decrees, is already obtained according to the Mu'tazila, so why not seek it?
3
Understand the implication
Seeking religious benefits like faith implies that faith and disbelief come from Allah, which is the Ash'ari position.
It's a subtle argument: the very act of seeking faith acknowledges it is not in human power.
4
Consider worldly benefits
Worldly benefits are described as base (khasīsah) and should not be made a prerequisite for worship.
This reinforces the priority of the Hereafter.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
How many of your daily acts of worship are motivated by seeking worldly benefits (like comfort, status, or safety) rather than purely religious ends? Will you commit to purifying your intention in at least one act today?
